<b>pribilihiyu</b> <i>n</i> @privilege. <i>v</i> [A12] enjoy a privilege.
<i>Tagsa ray táwung makapribilihiyu ug
sáma sa átung naangkun karun,</i> It's rare
for a person to get privileges of the sort we
are enjoying now.

<b>pribinir</b> <i>v</i> [A; b6(1)] set s.t. @aside for a purpose.
<i>Nakapribinir ka nag kwarta pára sa
ímung pagpanganak?</i> Have you set anything
aside for your delivery? <i>Pribinihi kug
dagkung púsù pára binhì,</i> Set some big ears
of corn aside for me for seedlings. <b>pribinídu</b>
<i>n</i> s.t. @{set aside}. <i>Pribinídu ning pagkaúna pára
sa kasíra,</i> This food has been set aside for
the boarder.

<b>pribyu</b> <i>n</i> a showing of a movie before its
normal run. <i>v</i> [A; c6] see a @preview showing
of a movie. <i>Mga kadagkúan[**-? F1: scratch] sa punduk
sibiku mauy mupribyu niánang salidáha,</i>
The heads of civic organizations will preview
that movie.

<b>prídi</b> <i>n</i> a k.o. popular @dance. <i>v</i> [A] do this
dance.

<b>pridikar</b> <i>v</i> [A; c] @preach the gospel. <i>Mupridikar
ang Murmun bísag lingiwlingíwan,</i>
The Mormons preach even if no one listens
to them.

<b>pridikt[va]r</b> <i>v</i> [A; a2b2] @foretell, @predict. <i>Íyang
hingpridiktahan ang súnug sa wà pa mahitabù,</i>
He predicted the fire before it happened.

<b>pridyidir</b> <i>n</i> @refrigerator. <i>v</i> <b>1</b> [A] use, own a
frigidaire. <b>2</b> [A; c] put s.t. in a frigidaire.
<i>Maprisirb[va]r ang pagkáun ug ipridyidir,</i> Food
keeps in the frigidaire.

<b>prigunta</b> <i>v</i> [A; ac] @ask s.o. a question, @inquire.
<i>Priguntahun ka gánì, sulti sa tinúud,</i>
If they question you, tell the truth. <i>Unsa
pay inyung iprigunta?</i> What else will you
ask? <i>n</i> @question.

<b>primíru</b> <i>n</i> <b>1</b> @first, @firstly. <i>Daghan kug balayran:
primíru, ang iskuylahan, sunud, ang kasíra,</i>
I have lots of payments to make: first,
the school, then, my board. <b>1a -- nga</b> [<i>verb</i>]
the first one that did, had [so-and-so] happen
to it. <i>Ang primírung makakità níya,</i>
The first one to see him. <i>Ang primírung masakpan,</i>
The first one caught. <b>2</b> first day of

March. <b>-- anyu</b> first year of college or high
school. <b>-- grádu</b> first grade. <b>-- upisiyal</b> chief
mate on a boat. <i>v</i> [B56] be, become first.
<i>Nagprimíru na ang Marsu ug wà pa si Makuy,</i>
Here it is the first of March, and Macoy
still hasn't come.[+]

<b>pungpung lálung</b> = <i>PUNGPUNG PYÁNGAW</i>,
<i>n</i>, <i>v.</i> <i>v</i> [A12C2] @{have sexual intercourse}

perspiring.

<b>pungpung pyángaw</b> <i>n</i> a game of the hands
played by children wherein the players put
their fists one on top of the other. A child
not participating is the leader <i>(abat)</i> and recites
a verse after which the fist at the bottom
opens; the verse is repeated and the
next fist opens, and so forth, until everybody
has opened his fist. Then the leader
inserts his index finger into the pile of
hands letting the players guess in turn if his
finger have touched bottom. The verse recited
goes: <i>Pungpung pyángaw, Bukadbukad
iláwum, Kulítug kulítug, Lagbas na ba?
Pungpung pyángaw,</i> Open up the lowest
hand, Thrust the finger in, Has it reached
the bottom? <i>v</i> [AC; c1] play <i>pungpung
pyángaw</i>.

<i>Puyra pungag nakabahù kug humut agwa sa

<b>ra</b> particle following the first word of a predicate.
<b>1</b> @only [predicate] and nothing else.
<i>Si Pidru ra ang mitábang nákù,</i> Pedro was
the only one that helped me. <i>Mau ray ákung
gianhi,</i> That is all I came to get. <i>Ginúu ray
mahibalu ug unsáun nà,</i> Only the Lord
knows what to do with that. <b>1a</b> [so-and-so]
did it himself. <i>Siya ray nag-unay sa íyang
anak,</i> He raped his own daughter. <b>1b</b> [<i>preposed
gen. pronoun</i>] <b>--</b> it is all my, your,
his, our, etc. very @own. <i>Ang mais, ímu ra
pud diayng abut?</i> Oh, is the corn your own
product, too? <b>1b1</b> <b>íya --</b> may this bad thing
happen only to him (phrase to ward off the
possibility that the bad thing may happen
to s.o. else). <i>Ag íyang úlu, íya ra, maáyung
pagkapusà,</i> He got his head completely
smashed--may it only happen to him. <b>1c</b>
<b>-- hinúun</b> <b>1c1</b> it's @merely, @only. <i>Sitinta ra
hinúun ning íyang ámut apan makatábang
ug tapal sa galastúhan,</i> He only contributed
seventy, but it can help cover the expenses.
<b>1c2</b> oh, it's nothing (said in modesty or
sarcastically about s.t. impressive). <i>Rulsruys
ra hinúun ang íyang awtu,</i> His car is only a
Rolls Royce. <b>2</b> @exactly [so-and-so]. <b>2a</b> with
measurements: [so-and-so much] and no
more. <i>Tulu ray makaadtu,</i> Only three people
can go. <b>2a1</b> with words referring to fitness,
sufficiency, preciseness: just exactly
@right, fitting, etc. <i>Hustu ra ning tulu,</i> Three
is just the right number. <i>Paríha ra ang duha,</i>
The two are @exactly alike. <i>Mahímù ra nang
gidak-úna,</i> That size will do perfectly. <b>2b</b>
<i>with words referring to location:</i> it is right
here, there. <i>Día ra ku,</i> I'm over here. <i>Náa
ra sa ímung atubángan,</i> There it is, right under
your nose. <b>2b1</b> no @further than [such-and-such
a place]. <i>Anhi ra kútub ang dálan,</i>
The road doesn't go any further than this.
<i>Didtu ra mi manáug,</i> We got off there and
went no further. <b>2b2</b> <b>anáa --</b> [<i>dat.</i>] it is @{up
to} [so-and-so]. <i>Náa ra níya ug mupalit ba
siya,</i> It is up to him if he wants to buy. <i>Náa
ra nímug mupadáyun ka,</i> It's entirely up to
you if you will continue. <b>2c</b> <b>mau -- ug, nga</b>
just exactly like, as if. <i>see</i> <sc>MAU</sc>, <i>3</i>, <i>4</i>. <b>2d</b> <b>maáyu
--</b> it would be just the right thing. <i>Maáyu
rag mamatay siya,</i> It would serve him
-----File: 1677.png--------------------------------------------------------
right if he died. <i>Maáyu rang napildi siya,</i>
Serves him right that he lost. (<i>see also</i> <b>3c</b>
<i>and</i> <b>4d</b>.) <b>3</b> [so-and-so] is certain to happen.
<i>Muanhi ra nà,</i> He'll come, don't worry. <i>May
adlaw rang gabáan ka,</i> The day will come
when you get yours. <i>Magkítà ra tag usab,</i>
We'll @surely see each other again. <b>3a</b> <b>-- gayud</b>
[so-and-so] will, did finally happen, @{despite
everything}. <i>Nakatápus ra giyud ku,</i> I finished,
despite everything. <i>Gimahalan ra giyud
mi sa tambal,</i> Much as we needed it, we
found the medicine too expensive. <b>3b</b> <b>bantug
--</b> @{no wonder}. <i>Bantug rang nagdalì. Mamisíta
diay siya,</i> No wonder he was in such
a rush. He wants to visit s.o. <b>3b1</b> <b>kanyáhay
--</b> @{no wonder} [such-and-such] a thing always
happens. <i>Kanyáhay rang dì padúul
nang batáa nímu, kay hingúsì ka,</i> No wonder
that child won't let you get near him.
You keep pinching him. <b>3c</b> <b>maáyu --</b> some
day it will be good for s.t. <i>Ayg ilábay kay
maáyu ra unyà nà,</i> Don't throw it away because
someday it will be of some use. <b>4</b>
[<i>adj.</i>] <b>--</b> <b>4a</b> @too or more [adj.] than satisfactory.
<i>Ang sapátus dakù ra kaáyu pára nákù,</i>
The shoes are too big for me. <b>4b</b> <i>with
adjectives indicating the smaller, the easier,
cheaper, lesser of two opposites:</i> only a
(small, light, short) very (easy, cheap, etc.).
<i>Kanang Tuway gamay ra nang baryúha,</i> Toway
is just a small barrio. <i>A, sayun ra kaáyu,</i>
Oh, it's so easy. <b>4b1</b> <b>láin, lahì --</b> very
much @different. <i>Lahì ra ang ímung batásan
kay sa ákù,</i> Your ways are very different
from mine. <b>subra --</b> much too much. <i>Subra
ra ang ímung gihátag,</i> You gave much too
much. <b>4b2</b> <b>layù --, walà --</b> very far @behind
in, not anywhere near as good as. <i>Ang inyung
balay layù ra sa ámù,</i> Your house isn't
anywhere near as nice as ours. <i>Walà ka ra sa
kumingking itandì nákù,</i> You're nothing
compared to me--not even up to my little
finger. <b>4c</b> <b>sámuk --</b> leave me be. (You're
too much of a nuisance.) <i>Sámuk ra. Magtuun
ku,</i> Leave me alone. I want to study.
<b>4d maáyu --</b> very @nice. <i>Maáyu rang ipakung
nang úlu mu sa bungbung,</i> How nice it
would be to smash your head against the
wall. <b>5</b> <i>with imperatives:</i> particle taking
-----File: 1678.png--------------------------------------------------------
the abruptness out of a command but definitely
a command given to s.o. who doesn't
have the right to refuse. <i>Ambi ra nang kutsilyu,</i>
Let me have that knife. <b>5a</b> <b>-- ugud</b> =
<b>RA</b>, <i>5</i>[**F2 <b><i>5</i></b> ?], but with slightly less curtness. <i>Kuháa
ra gud ri,</i> Would you come get this, please.
<b>5b</b> <b>tan-áwa --, -- gud</b> can you beat that!
<i>Tan-áwa ra, siyay nangúna siya pay nangísug,</i>
Take a look at that! He started it and
now he gets mad! <b>5c</b> <b>-- gánì</b> go on now
and do [so-and-so]. <b>Lakaw ra ngánì kay
dúru na nílang paábut,</b> Go on now. They
have been waiting forever. <i>Ayaw ra gánì nag
garùgarúa,</i> Stop jiggling that. You know
you shouldn't. <b>6</b> <b>yátì, yáwà, yátis --</b> I don't
believe it. <i>Kadaug kas swipstik? Yátì ra!</i>
You won the sweepstakes? I don't believe
it. <b>6a</b> in accepting a challenge: I don't believe
you dare challenge me! <i>Yátì ra! Makigsumbagay
ka nàkù?</i> You mean to say
you dare challenge me to a fight? <b>7</b> <b>-- ba</b>
<b>7a</b> particle with a reason which is given as
advice or warning. <i>Higúpa dáyun kay ínit
pa ra ba,</i> Eat it right away because it's still
warm. <i>Mangísug ra ba tug madúgay ka,</i> He
will get angry if you take too long. <b>7b</b> ordinarily
[so-and-so] would have been OK,
but ... <i>Sus, nía na ang mga bisíta. Wà ra ba
tay giandam,</i> My! The visitors have arrived
and here we don't have anything to give
them. <i>Dà, nag-uwan na hinúun. Wà ra ba
kuy páyung,</i> Darn! It's raining, and I don't
have an umbrella. <b>7c</b> particle with an apology.
<i>Wà ra ba diri si Nánay,</i> I'm @sorry, Mom's
not here.

<b>sa_{1}</b> particle indicating grammatical relations.
<i>short form:</i> <b>s</b>. <b>1</b> preceding a phrase referring
to a place. <i>Niadtu sa Manílà,</i> Went to
Manila. <i>Sa ibabaw,</i> Up on top. <i>Lakaw
ngadtu sa unáhan,</i> Walk up ahead. <i>Ihátag
sa bátà,</i> Give it to the child. <i>Nahúlug sa
pangpang,</i> Fell off the cliff. <i>Amíhan sa
kanáway,</i> Northwind from a westerly direction.
<b>1a</b> following a word meaning 'be
in a place'. <i>Nia dinhi sa Sibu,</i> It is here in
Cebu. <i>Didtu siya sa Manílà iskuyla,</i> He
went to school in Manila. <i>Walà sa lugar,</i>
Not at the right time or place. <b>2</b> preceding
a phrase referring to time. <i>Muanhi sa alas
dúsi,</i> Will come at twelve. <i>Malígù ta sa
sunud Duminggu,</i> Let's go swimming next
Sunday. <i>Sa káda ámut mutugbang pud
siyag hátag,</i> Each time they contribute, he
gives an equal amount. <b>2a</b> preceding a sentence
referring to past time. <i>Sa pag-abut na
níya didtu,</i> When he arrived there. <i>Sa nagalakat
ang panahun,</i> As time went by. <b>3</b> indicating
gen. relations. <b>3a</b> possession or
analogous concepts. <i>Ang balay sa ákung amígu,</i>
My friend's house. <i>Ang mga pagtulun-an
sa Bibliya,</i> The lessons given in the
Bible. <i>Ang sa ákung mga igsúun,</i> The ones
belonging to my brothers and sisters. <i>Usa sa
ákung mga sákup,</i> One of my people. <i>Ang
kamahal sa palalítun,</i> The high cost of things.
-----File: 1709.png--------------------------------------------------------
<i>Búlan sa Máyu,</i> The month of May. <b>3b</b> agent
of a passive verb. <i>Gihambat sa liyun,</i> Was devoured
by the lion. <i>Kaúnun sa mga bátà,</i> The
children will eat it. <b>3b1</b> preceding the agent
of a nominalized verb. <i>Ang pagkamatay sa
bátà,</i> When the child died (lit. the dying of
the child). <i>Káda kanáug sa pasahíru,</i> Each
time a passenger got off. (Lit. Each getting
off of the passengers.) <b>3c</b> following an exclamation
to mark the thing exclaimed over.
[** doubled line which][** mation to mark the thing exclaimed over. -Deleted][**corrected typo]
<i>Kamahal gud sa ímung gibáyad!</i> What a high
price you paid! <i>Dakúa sad sa balay!</i> What
a huge house it was! <b>4</b> indicating dat. relations.
<b>4a</b> specific goal of an action. <i>Nakabunù
sa íyang kaáway,</i> Killed his enemy. <i>Akuy
gitagáan sa libru,</i> The book was given to me.
<b>4b</b> <i>in comparisons:</i> @than. <i>Dátù pa sa ákung
amahan,</i> Richer than my father. <b>4c</b> <i>-- ákù, ímu,
íya, ámù, átù, inyu, íla</i> = <sc>KANÁMÙ, KANÍMU,
KANÍYA, KANÁMÙ, KANÁTÙ, KANINYU,
KANÍLA</sc>. <b>5</b> indicating causal, instrumental,
or concommitant[**spellcheck: concomitant? P2] relations. <i>Mihílak
sa kapungut,</i> Cried out of anger. <i>Sa tantung
paningkámut, milampus,</i> He succeeded after
trying so hard. <i>Íyang gisuntuk sa walang
kamut,</i> He hit him with his left hand. <i>Sa minaayug
sa dinautan,</i> By hook or by crook.
<i>Sapátus nga naghilíra sa kadaghan,</i> Rows
and rows of shoes, there were so many of
-----File: 1710.png--------------------------------------------------------
them. <i>Mitandù sa walay lángan,</i> He agreed
without delay. <b>5a</b> following a word which
expresses these relationships. <i>Báhin sa ákung
hangyù,</i> As for my request. <i>Tungud
sa kalúuy,</i> On account of his mercy. <i>Uban
sa íyang amahan,</i> Together with her father.
<i>Para ni sa Nága?</i> Is this bound for Naga?
<i>Human sa klási,</i> After class. <b>6</b> optionally
preceding an infinitive with <i>pag</i>-. <i>Arun sa
pagpauswag sa lungsud,</i> In order to develop
the town. <i>Misúgud na sad siya sa pag-inum,</i>
He began to take to the bottle again.
